       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Between 1993 and 2003, many rounds of peace talks, overseen by regional leaders in Tanzania, South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, gradually established power-sharing agreements to satisfy the majority of the contending groups. Initially the South African Protection Support Detachment was deployed to protect Burundian leaders returning from exile. These forces became part of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_in_Burundi" title="African Union Mission in Burundi">African Union Mission to Burundi</a>, deployed to help oversee the installation of a transitional government. In June 2004, the UN stepped in and took over peacekeeping responsibilities as a signal of growing international support for the already markedly advanced peace process in Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The mission's mandate, under <a href="/wiki/Chapter_VII_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter VII of the United Nations Charter">Chapter VII of the United Nations Charter</a>, has been to monitor cease-fire; carry out disarmament, demobilisation and reintegration of former combatants; support humanitarian assistance and refugee and IDP return; assist with elections; protect international staff and Burundian civilians; monitor Burundi's troublesome borders, including halting illicit arms flows; and assist in carrying out institutional reforms including those of the Constitution, judiciary, armed forces and police. The mission has been allotted 5,650 military personnel, 120 civilian police and about 1,000 international and local civilian personnel. The mission has been functioning well. It has greatly benefited from the transitional government, which has functioned and is in the process of transitioning to one that will be popularly elected.<sup id="cite_ref-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The main difficulty in the early stages was continued resistance to the peace process by the last Hutu nationalist rebel group. This organisation continued its violent conflict on the outskirts of the capital despite the UN's presence. By June 2005, the group had stopped fighting and its representatives were brought back into the political process. All political parties have accepted a formula for inter-ethnic power-sharing: no political party can gain access to government offices unless it is ethnically integrated.<sup id="cite_ref-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The focus of the UN's mission had been to enshrine the power-sharing arrangements in a popularly voted constitution, so that elections may be held and a new government installed. Disarmament, demobilisation and reintegration were done in tandem with elections preparations. In February 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Burundi" title="Constitution of Burundi">constitution</a> was approved with over 90% of the popular vote. In May, June and August 2005, three separate elections were also held at the local level for the Parliament and the presidency. </p>
      <p>While there are still some difficulties with refugee returns and securing adequate food supplies for the war-weary population, the mission managed to win the trust and confidence of a majority of the formerly warring leaders, as well as the population at large.<sup id="cite_ref-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard,_Lise_Morje_2008-66">[65]</a></sup> It was involved with several "quick effect" projects, including rehabilitating and building schools, orphanages, health clinics and rebuilding infrastructure such as water lines. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_to_2018">2006 to 2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2006 to 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="aerial view of highrise building and low rise red roofed buildings" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg/220px-BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg/330px-BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg/440px-BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BujumburaFromCathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>View of the capital city Bujumbura in 2006.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Reconstruction efforts in Burundi started to practically take effect after 2006. The UN shut down its peacekeeping mission and re-focused on helping with reconstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-accessed_on_29-10-08_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accessed_on_29-10-08-67">[66]</a></sup> Toward achieving <a href="/wiki/Economic_reconstruction" title="Economic reconstruction">economic reconstruction</a>, Rwanda, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">D.R.Congo</a> and Burundi relaunched the regional <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_the_Great_Lakes_Countries" title="Economic Community of the Great Lakes Countries">Economic Community of the Great Lakes Countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-accessed_on_29-10-08_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accessed_on_29-10-08-67">[66]</a></sup> In addition, Burundi, along with Rwanda, joined the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> in 2007. </p>
      <p>However, the terms of the September 2006 Ceasefire between the government and the last remaining armed opposition group, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Burundi)" title="National Liberation Front (Burundi)">FLN</a> (Forces for National Liberation, also called NLF or FROLINA), were not totally implemented, and senior FLN members subsequently left the truce monitoring team, claiming that their security was threatened.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In September 2007, rival FLN factions clashed in the capital, killing 20 fighters and causing residents to begin fleeing. Rebel raids were reported in other parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-accessed_on_29-10-08_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accessed_on_29-10-08-67">[66]</a></sup> The rebel factions disagreed with the government over disarmament and the release of political prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-69">[68]</a></sup> In late 2007 and early 2008, FLN combatants attacked government-protected camps where former combatants were living. The homes of rural residents were also pillaged.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-69">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2007 report<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-69">[68]</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> mentions many areas where improvement is required. Civilians are victims of repeated acts of violence done by the FLN. The latter also recruits child soldiers. The rate of violence against women is high. Perpetrators regularly escape prosecution and punishment by the state. There is an urgent need for reform of the judicial system. <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">Genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> remain unpunished. The establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Truth_and_Reconciliation_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Truth and Reconciliation Commission">Truth and Reconciliation Commission</a> and a Special <a href="/wiki/Tribunal" title="Tribunal">Tribunal</a> for investigation and prosecution has not yet been implemented. The freedom of expression is limited; journalists are frequently arrested for carrying out legitimate professional activities. A total of 38,087 Burundian refugees have been repatriated between January and November 2007. </p>
      <p>In late March 2008, the FLN sought for the parliament to adopt a law guaranteeing them 'provisional immunity' from arrest. This would cover ordinary crimes, but not grave violations of international humanitarian law like war crimes or crimes against humanity .<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-69">[68]</a></sup> Even though the government has granted this in the past to people, the FLN has been unable to obtain the provisional immunity. </p>
      <p>On 17 April 2008, the FLN bombarded Bujumbura. The Burundian army fought back and the FLN suffered heavy losses. A new ceasefire was signed on 26 May 2008. In August 2008, President Nkurunziza met with the FLN leader <a href="/wiki/Agathon_Rwasa" title="Agathon Rwasa">Agathon Rwasa</a>, with the mediation of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nqakula" title="Charles Nqakula">Charles Nqakula</a>, South Africa's Minister for Safety and Security. This was the first direct meeting since June 2007. Both agreed to meet twice a week to establish a commission to resolve any disputes that might arise during the peace negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Refugee camps are now closing down and 450,000 refugees have returned. The economy of the country is shattered – as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Burundi has one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">per capita gross incomes</a> in the world. With the return of refugees, amongst others, property conflicts have started. </p>
      <p>Burundi now participates in African Union peacekeeping missions, including the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia" title="African Union Mission to Somalia">mission to Somalia</a> against Al-Shabaab militants.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_unrest">2015 unrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2015 unrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burundian_unrest_(2015%E2%80%932018)" title="Burundian unrest (2015–2018)">Burundian unrest (2015–2018)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In April 2015 protests broke out after the ruling party announced President <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Nkurunziza" title="Pierre Nkurunziza">Pierre Nkurunziza</a> would seek a third term in office.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> Protestors claimed Nkurunziza could not run for a third term in office but the country's constitutional court agreed with the President (although some of its members had fled the country at the time of its vote).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2015_Burundian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2015 Burundian coup d'état attempt">An attempted coup d'état on 13 May</a> failed to depose Nkurunziza. <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> He returned to Burundi, began purging his government, and arrested several of the coup leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn01_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn01-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> Following the attempted coup, protests however continued and over 100,000 people had fled the country by 20 May causing a humanitarian emergency. There are reports of continued and widespread abuses of human rights, including unlawful killings, torture, disappearances, and restrictions on freedom of expression.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite calls by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, and various other governments, the ruling party <a href="/wiki/Burundian_legislative_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Burundian legislative election, 2015">held parliamentary elections on 29 June</a>, but these were boycotted by the opposition. </p>
      <p>On 30 September 2016, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> established the Commission of Inquiry on Burundi through resolution 33/24. Its mandate is to "conduct a thorough investigation into human rights violations and abuses committed in Burundi since April 2015, to identify alleged perpetrators and to formulate recommendations."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> On 29 September 2017 the Commission of Inquiry on Burundi called on Burundian government to put an end to serious <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights violations">human rights violations</a>. It further stressed that, "The Burundian government has so far refused to cooperate with the Commission of Inquiry, despite the Commission's repeated requests and initiatives."<sup id="cite_ref-ohchr.org_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohchr.org-84">[83]</a></sup> The violations the Commission documented include <a href="/wiki/Arrests" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrests">arbitrary arrests</a> and detentions, acts of <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> and cruel, <a href="/wiki/Inhuman_or_degrading_treatment" title="Inhuman or degrading treatment">inhuman or degrading treatment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_execution" class="mw-redirect" title="Extrajudicial execution">extrajudicial executions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enforced_disappearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Enforced disappearances">enforced disappearances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> and other forms of sexual violence."<sup id="cite_ref-ohchr.org_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohchr.org-84">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_to_present">2018 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2018 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In a <a href="/wiki/2018_Burundian_constitutional_referendum" title="2018 Burundian constitutional referendum">constitutional referendum</a> in May 2018, Burundians voted by 79.08% to approve an amended constitution that ensured that Nkurunziza could remain in power until 2034.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> However, much to the surprise of most observers, Nkurunziza later announced that he did not intend to serve another term, paving the way for a new president to be elected in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Burundian_general_election" title="2020 Burundian general election">2020 General Election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 May 2020, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89variste_Ndayishimiye" title="Évariste Ndayishimiye">Evariste Ndayishimiye</a>, a candidate who was hand-picked as Nkurunziza's successor by the CNDD-FDD, won the election with 71.45% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-88">[87]</a></sup> Shortly after, on 9 June 2020, Nkurunziza died of a cardiac arrest, at the age of 55.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-87">[86]</a></sup> There was some speculation that his death was COVID-19 related, though this is unconfirmed.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> As per the constitution, <a href="/wiki/Pascal_Nyabenda" title="Pascal Nyabenda">Pascal Nyabenda</a>, the president of the national assembly, led the government until Ndayishimiye's inauguration on 18 June 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-88">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Burundi" title="Politics of Burundi">Politics of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pierre Nkurunziza at World Economic Forum 2008 looking right" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg/220px-Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="329" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg/330px-Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg/440px-Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="669" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pierre_Nkurunziza_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Africa_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Nkurunziza" title="Pierre Nkurunziza">Pierre Nkurunziza</a>, President of Burundi in 2005–2020.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi's political system is that of a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic based upon a multi-party state. The President of Burundi is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. There are currently 21 <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Burundi" title="List of political parties in Burundi">registered parties in Burundi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> On 13 March 1992, Tutsi coup leader <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Buyoya" title="Pierre Buyoya">Pierre Buyoya</a> established a constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated8_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated8-16">[15]</a></sup> which provided for a multi-party political process and reflected multi-party competition.<sup id="cite_ref-PH_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH-17">[16]</a></sup> Six years later, on 6 June 1998, the constitution was changed, broadening <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Burundi" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Burundi">National Assembly</a>'s seats and making provisions for two vice-presidents. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Accords_(Burundi)" title="Arusha Accords (Burundi)">Arusha Accord</a>, Burundi enacted a transitional government in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-unburundi_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unburundi-18">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burundi's legislative branch is a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> assembly, consisting of the Transitional National Assembly and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Burundi" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Burundi">Transitional Senate</a>. As of 2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Transitional National Assembly consisted of 170 members, with the Front for Democracy in Burundi holding 38% of seats, and 10% of the assembly controlled by UPRONA. Fifty-two seats were controlled by other parties. Burundi's constitution mandates representation in the Transitional National Assembly to be consistent with 60% Hutu, 40% Tutsi, and 30% female members, as well as three Batwa members.<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> Members of the National Assembly are elected by popular vote and serve five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-Puddington_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington-90">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Transitional Senate has fifty-one members, and three seats are reserved for former presidents. Due to stipulations in Burundi's constitution, 30% of Senate members must be female. Members of the Senate are elected by electoral colleges, which consist of members from each of Burundi's provinces and communes.<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> For each of Burundi's eighteen provinces, one Hutu and one Tutsi senator are chosen. One term for the Transitional Senate is five years.<sup id="cite_ref-Puddington_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington-90">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Together, Burundi's legislative branch elect the President to a five-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-Puddington_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington-90">[89]</a></sup> Burundi's president appoints officials to his Council of Ministers, which is also part of the executive branch.<sup id="cite_ref-unburundi_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unburundi-18">[17]</a></sup> The president can also pick fourteen members of the Transitional Senate to serve on the Council of Ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> Members of the Council of Ministers must be approved by two-thirds of Burundi's legislature. The president also chooses two vice-presidents.<sup id="cite_ref-Puddington_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington-90">[89]</a></sup> Following the 2015 election, the President of Burundi was <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Nkurunziza" title="Pierre Nkurunziza">Pierre Nkurunziza</a>. The First Vice-President was Therence Sinunguruza, and the Second Vice-President was Gervais Rufyikiri.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 May 2020, <a href="/wiki/Evariste_Ndayishimiye" class="mw-redirect" title="Evariste Ndayishimiye">Evariste Ndayishimiye</a>, a candidate who was hand-picked as Nkurunziza's successor by the CNDD-FDD, won <a href="/wiki/2020_Burundian_general_election" title="2020 Burundian general election">the election</a> with 71.45% of the vote. Shortly after, on 9 June 2020, Nkurunziza died of a cardiac arrest, at the age of 55.As per the constitution, Pascal Nyabenda, the president of the national assembly, led the government until Ndayishimiye's inauguration on 18 June 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>Cour Suprême</i> (Supreme Court) is Burundi's highest court. There are three Courts of Appeals directly below the Supreme Court. Tribunals of First Instance are used as judicial courts in each of Burundi's provinces as well as 123 local tribunals.<sup id="cite_ref-unburundi_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unburundi-18">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Burundi" title="Human rights in Burundi">Human rights in Burundi</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Burundi" title="LGBT rights in Burundi">LGBT rights in Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi's government has been repeatedly criticised by human rights organisations including <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> for the multiple arrests and trials of journalist <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Kavumbagu" title="Jean-Claude Kavumbagu">Jean-Claude Kavumbagu</a> for issues related to his reporting. <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> (AI) named him a <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoner of conscience</a> and called for his "immediate and unconditional release." </p>
      <p>In April 2009, the government of Burundi changed the law to criminalise <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a>. Persons found guilty of consensual same-sex relations risk two to three years in prison and a fine of 50,000 to 100,000 Burundian francs.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> Amnesty International has condemned the action, calling it a violation of Burundi's obligations under international and regional human rights law, and against the constitution, which guarantees the right to privacy.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Punctuation" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="Quotation marks may be incomplete, unbalanced or improperly applied.">check quotation syntax</span></a></i>]</sup> Burundi officially left the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> (ICC) on 27 October 2017, the first country in the world to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-97">[96]</a></sup> The move came after the UN accused the country of various crimes and human rights violations, such as extrajudicial killings, torture and sexual violence, in a September 2017 report.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-97">[96]</a></sup> The ICC announced on 9 November 2017 that human rights violations from the time Burundi was a member would still be prosecuted.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burundi" title="Provinces of Burundi">Provinces of Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Burundi" title="Communes of Burundi">Communes of Burundi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Collines_of_Burundi" title="Collines of Burundi">Collines of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi is divided into 18 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burundi" title="Provinces of Burundi">provinces</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-statoids_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoids-100">[99]</a></sup> 117 <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Burundi" title="Communes of Burundi">communes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> and 2,638 <a href="/wiki/Collines_of_Burundi" title="Collines of Burundi">collines</a> (hills).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Provincial governments are structured upon these boundaries. In 2000, the province encompassing Bujumbura was separated into two provinces, Bujumbura Rural and Bujumbura Mairie.<sup id="cite_ref-xlix_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xlix-14">[13]</a></sup> The newest province, <a href="/wiki/Rumonge_Province" title="Rumonge Province">Rumonge</a>, was created on 26 March 2015 from portions of Bujumbura Rural and Bururi.<sup id="cite_ref-rumong_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rumong-102">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div>

      <p><br> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:By-map.png" class="image"><img alt="tan colour map of Burundi with cities" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/By-map.png/220px-By-map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/By-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="329"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:By-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Burundi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Burundi" title="Geography of Burundi">Geography of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burundi_Hillside.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Burundi_Hillside.png/220px-Burundi_Hillside.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Burundi_Hillside.png/330px-Burundi_Hillside.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Burundi_Hillside.png/440px-Burundi_Hillside.png 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="4608"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burundi_Hillside.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Deforestation South of Bubanzi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>One of the smallest countries in Africa, Burundi is landlocked and has an <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">equatorial climate</a>. Burundi is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a>, the western extension of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>. The country lies on a rolling <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> in the centre of Africa. Burundi is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the east and southeast, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the west. It lies within the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift_montane_forests" title="Albertine Rift montane forests">Albertine Rift montane forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Zambezian_miombo_woodlands" title="Central Zambezian miombo woodlands">Central Zambezian miombo woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Basin_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Basin forest-savanna mosaic">Victoria Basin forest-savanna mosaic</a> ecoregions.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-104">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The average elevation of the central plateau is 1,707&nbsp;m (5,600&nbsp;ft), with lower elevations at the borders. The highest peak, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Heha" title="Mount Heha">Mount Heha</a> at 2,685&nbsp;m (8,810&nbsp;ft),<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-105">[104]</a></sup> lies to the southeast of the largest city and economic capital, Bujumbura. The source of the <a href="/wiki/Nile_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile River">Nile River</a> is in Bururi province, and is linked from Lake Victoria to its headwaters via the <a href="/wiki/Ruvyironza_River" title="Ruvyironza River">Ruvyironza River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated9_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated9-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> is also an important water source, which serves as a fork to the <a href="/wiki/Kagera_River" title="Kagera River">Kagera River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Another major lake is <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>, located in much of Burundi's southwestern corner.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-109">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are two <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kibira_National_Park" title="Kibira National Park">Kibira National Park</a> to the northwest (a small region of rainforest, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Nyungwe_Forest_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyungwe Forest National Park">Nyungwe Forest National Park</a> in Rwanda), <a href="/wiki/Ruvubu_National_Park" title="Ruvubu National Park">Ruvubu National Park</a> to the northeast (along the <a href="/wiki/Rurubu_River" title="Rurubu River">Rurubu River</a>, also known as Ruvubu or Ruvuvu). Both were established in 1982 to conserve wildlife populations.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-110">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Burundi" title="Economy of Burundi">Economy of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Burundi" class="mw-redirect" title="List of companies based in Burundi">List of companies based in Burundi</a>
      </div>
      <p>Burundi is a landlocked, resource-poor country with an underdeveloped manufacturing sector. The economy is predominantly agricultural, accounting for 50% of GDP in 2017<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> and employing more than 90% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">Subsistence agriculture</a> accounts for 90% of agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-112">[111]</a></sup> Burundi's primary exports are coffee and tea, which account for 90% of foreign exchange earnings, though exports are a relatively small share of GDP. Other agricultural products include cotton, tea, maize, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, sweet potatoes, bananas, <a href="/wiki/Manioc" class="mw-redirect" title="Manioc">manioc</a> (tapioca); beef, milk and hides. Even though <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence farming</a> is highly relied upon, many people do not have the resources to sustain themselves. This is due to large population growth and no coherent policies governing land ownership. In 2014, the average farm size was about one acre. Burundi is one of the world's poorest countries, owing in part to its landlocked geography,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-7">[6]</a></sup> poor legal system, lack of economic freedom, lack of access to education and the proliferation of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>. Approximately 80% of Burundi's population lives in poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> Famines and food shortages have occurred throughout Burundi, most notably in the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-wein5_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wein5-36">[35]</a></sup> and according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, 56.8% of children under age five suffer from chronic <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> Burundi's export earnings – and its ability to pay for imports – rests primarily on weather conditions and international coffee and tea prices.</p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="color chart of exports by value with percentages" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burundi.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Burundi's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The purchasing power of most Burundians has decreased as wage increases have not kept up with inflation. As a result of deepening poverty, Burundi will remain heavily dependent on aid from bilateral and multilateral donors. Foreign aid represents 42% of Burundis national income, the second highest rate in Sub-Saharan Africa. Burundi joined the East African Community in 2009, which should boost its regional trade ties, and also in 2009 received $700 million in debt relief. Government corruption is hindering the development of a healthy private sector as companies seek to navigate an environment with ever-changing rules.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-7">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Studies since 2007 have shown Burundians to have extremely poor levels of <a href="/wiki/Satisfaction_with_Life_Index" title="Satisfaction with Life Index">satisfaction with life</a>; the <a href="/wiki/World_Happiness_Report" title="World Happiness Report">World Happiness Report 2018</a> rated them the world's least happy in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg" class="image"><img alt="two sitting in skiff on beach on lakeshore with mountains in bckround" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg/220px-Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg/330px-Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg/440px-Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burundi_-_Lake_Tanganyika_fisheries.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fishermen on Lake Tanganyika.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Some of Burundi's natural resources include <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, nickel, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">platinum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Besides agriculture, other industries include: assembly of imported components; public works construction; food processing and light consumer goods such as blankets, shoes and soap. </p>
      <p>In regards to telecommunications infrastructure, Burundi is ranked 2nd to last in the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>'s Network Readiness Index (NRI) – an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Burundi ranked number 147 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, down from 144 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lack of access to financial services is a serious problem for the majority of the population, particularly in the densely populated rural areas: only 2% of the total population holds bank accounts, and fewer than 0.5% use bank lending services. <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">Microfinance</a>, however, plays a larger role, with 4% of Burundians being members of microfinance institutions – a larger share of the population than that reached by banking and postal services combined. 26 licensed microfinance institutions (MFIs) offer savings, deposits and short- to medium-term credit. Dependence of the sector on donor assistance is limited.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burundi is part of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> and a potential member of the planned <a href="/wiki/East_African_Federation" title="East African Federation">East African Federation</a>. Economic growth in Burundi is relatively steady but Burundi is still behind neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Currency">Currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burundian_Franc" class="mw-redirect" title="Burundian Franc">Burundian Franc</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Burundian_franc" title="Burundian franc">Burundian franc</a> (ISO 4217 code BIF). It is nominally subdivided into 100 <a href="/wiki/Centime" title="Centime">centimes</a>, though coins have never been issued in centimes in independent Burundi; centime coins were circulated only when Burundi used the <a href="/wiki/Congolese_franc" title="Congolese franc">Belgian Congo franc</a>. </p>
      <p>Monetary Policy is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Burundi" title="Bank of the Republic of Burundi">Bank of the Republic of Burundi</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Burundi" title="Transport in Burundi">Transport in Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega,_Burundi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="two bicyclists hold on to back of truck descending a hill" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg/220px-Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg/330px-Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg/440px-Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega%2C_Burundi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2162" data-file-height="1147"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Truck_and_bicylists_near_Gitega,_Burundi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bicycles are a popular means of transport in Burundi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi's transport network is limited and underdeveloped. According to a 2012 <i>DHL Global Connectedness Index</i>, Burundi is the least globalised of 140 surveyed countries.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bujumbura_International_Airport" title="Bujumbura International Airport">Bujumbura International Airport</a> is the only airport with a paved runway and as of May 2017 it was serviced by four airlines (<a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">Ethiopian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/RwandAir" title="RwandAir">RwandAir</a>). <a href="/wiki/Kigali_International_Airport" title="Kigali International Airport">Kigali</a> is the city with the most daily flight connections to Bujumbura. The country has a road network but as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> less than 10% of the country's roads were paved and as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> private bus companies were the main operators of buses on the international route to Kigali; however, there were no bus connections to the other neighbouring countries (Tanzania and the Democratic Republic of Congo).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Bujumbura is connected by a passenger and cargo ferry (the <a href="/wiki/MV_Mwongozo" title="MV Mwongozo">MV Mwongozo</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Kigoma" title="Kigoma">Kigoma</a> in Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> There is a <a href="/wiki/East_African_Railway_Master_Plan" title="East African Railway Master Plan">long-term plan</a> to link the country via rail to Kigali and then onward to Kampala and Kenya. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg" class="image"><img alt="women in colourful dresses tending goats" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg/220px-Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg/330px-Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg/440px-Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karuzi_Burundi_goats.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A group of Burundian women rearing goats.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg" class="image"><img alt="three children looking directly at camera" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg/220px-Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg/330px-Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg/440px-Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Bujumbura.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Children in Bujumbura, Burundi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Burundi" title="Demographics of Burundi">Demographics of Burundi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Burundi" title="Languages of Burundi">Languages of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of July 2018, Burundi was estimated by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs#Divisions" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations</a> to have a population of 11,175,374 people,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-124">[123]</a></sup> compared to only 2,456,000 in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Population_growth_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Population growth rate">population growth rate</a> is 2.5 percent per year, more than double the average global pace, and a Burundian woman has on average 6.3 children, nearly triple the international <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FP-March_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FP-March-126">[125]</a></sup> Burundi had the fifth highest <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in the world in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-7">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many Burundians have migrated to other countries as a result of the civil war. In 2006, the United States accepted approximately 10,000 Burundian refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burundi remains an overwhelmingly rural society, with just 13% of the population living in urban areas in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-7">[6]</a></sup> The population density of around 315 people per square kilometre (753 per sq&nbsp;mi) is the second highest in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-15">[14]</a></sup> Roughly 85% of the population are of <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> ethnic origin, 15% are <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> and fewer than 1% are indigenous <a href="/wiki/Twa" title="Twa">Twa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-20">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of Burundi are <a href="/wiki/Kirundi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kirundi language">Kirundi</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. </p>
      <p><br> </p>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">9</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Karuzi" title="Karuzi">Karuzi</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Karuzi" title="Karuzi">Karuzi</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">10,317 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kirundo" title="Kirundo">Kirundo</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kirundo" title="Kirundo">Kirundo</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">10,024 </td>

      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Burundi" title="Religion in Burundi">Religion in Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Burundi" title="Religion in Burundi">Religion in Burundi</a><sup id="cite_ref-pew_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-129">[128]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Burundi" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Burundi">Catholic</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:yellow; width:65%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">65%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Burundi" title="Christianity in Burundi">Protestant</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:blue; width:26%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">26%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Folk</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:red; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Burundi" title="Islam in Burundi">Muslim</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Burundi" title="Freedom of religion in Burundi">Other</a></td>

            <div style="background:grey; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td>

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">None</a></td>

            <div style="background:black; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Sources estimate the Christian population at 80–90%, with Roman Catholics representing the largest group at 60–65%. <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> practitioners constitute the remaining 15–25%. An estimated 5% of the population adheres to traditional indigenous religious beliefs. Muslims constitute 2–5%, the majority of whom are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunnis</a> and live in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pew_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-129">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-state2010_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state2010-130">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Burundi" title="Health in Burundi">Health in Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi has the severest hunger and malnourishment rates of all 120 countries ranked in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FP-March_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FP-March-126">[125]</a></sup> The civil war in 1962 put a stop on the medical advancements in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-131">[130]</a></sup> Burundi, again, went into a violent cycle in 2015, jeopardising the citizens of Burundi's medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-132">[131]</a></sup> Like many Sub-Saharan Africa countries, Burundi uses indigenous medicine in addition to biomedicine. In the 1980s Burundi's health authorities asked the United Nations Development Program for support to develop quality control and begin new research on pharmaceuticals from medicinal plants.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-131">[130]</a></sup> At the same time, the Burundi Association of Traditional Practitioners (ATRADIBU) was founded, which teamed up with the governments agency to set up the Centre for Research and Promotion of Traditional Medicine in Burundi (CRPMT).<sup id="cite_ref-:4_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-131">[130]</a></sup> The recent influx of international aid has supported the work of biomedical health systems in Burundi. However, international aid workers have traditionally stayed away from indigenous medicine in Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-131">[130]</a></sup> As of 2015, roughly 1 out of 10 children in Burundi die before the age of 5 from preventable and treatable illnesses such as pneumonia, diarrhoea, and malaria.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-132">[131]</a></sup> The current violence in Burundi has limited the country's access to medication and hospital equipment. Burundi's life expectancy, as of 2015, was 60.1 years.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-133">[132]</a></sup> In 2013, Burundi spent 8% of their GDP on healthcare.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-133">[132]</a></sup> While Burundi's fertility rate is 6.1 children per women, the country's mortality rate is 61.9 deaths for every 1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-133">[132]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a>, the average life expectancy in the country is 58/62 years.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> Common diseases in Burundi include malaria and typhoid fever.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-133">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gitega_drums.JPG" class="image"><img alt="four drums in courtyard" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Gitega_drums.JPG/220px-Gitega_drums.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Gitega_drums.JPG/330px-Gitega_drums.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Gitega_drums.JPG/440px-Gitega_drums.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gitega_drums.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Drums from <a href="/wiki/Gitega" title="Gitega">Gitega</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Burundi" title="Culture of Burundi">Culture of Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Burundi" title="Tourism in Burundi">Tourism in Burundi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Burundi" title="Music of Burundi">Music of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burundi's culture is based on local tradition and the influence of neighbouring countries, though cultural prominence has been hindered by <a href="/wiki/Civil_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil unrest">civil unrest</a>. Since farming is the main industry, a typical Burundian meal consists of <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pea" title="Pea">peas</a>. Due to the expense, meat is eaten only a few times per month. </p>
      <p>When several Burundians of close acquaintance meet for a gathering they drink <i>impeke</i>, a beer, together from a large container to symbolise unity.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Notable Burundians include the footballer <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Tchit%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed Tchité">Mohammed Tchité</a> and singer <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Nimbona" title="Jean-Pierre Nimbona">Jean-Pierre Nimbona</a>, popularly known as Kidumu (who is based in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, Kenya). </p>
      <p>Crafts are an important art form in Burundi and are attractive gifts to many tourists. Basket weaving is a popular craft for local artisans.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> Other crafts such as masks, shields, statues and pottery are made in Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-137">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Drumming is an important part of the cultural heritage. The world-famous <a href="/wiki/Royal_Drummers_of_Burundi" title="Royal Drummers of Burundi">Royal Drummers of Burundi</a>, who have performed for over 40 years, are noted for traditional drumming using the <a href="/wiki/Karyenda" title="Karyenda">karyenda</a>, amashako, ibishikiso and ikiranya drums.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Dance often accompanies drumming performance, which is frequently seen in celebrations and family gatherings. The abatimbo, which is performed at official ceremonies and rituals and the fast-paced abanyagasimbo are some famous Burundian dances. Some musical instruments of note are the flute, <a href="/wiki/Zither" title="Zither">zither</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ikembe" title="Ikembe">ikembe</a>, indonongo, <a href="/wiki/Umuduri" title="Umuduri">umuduri</a>, inanga and the inyagara.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-137">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Match.jpg" class="image"><img alt="five men playing football one red and black striped jersey and four in yellow jersey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Le_Match.jpg/220px-Le_Match.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Le_Match.jpg/330px-Le_Match.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Le_Match.jpg/440px-Le_Match.jpg 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Match.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Football in Burundi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral tradition</a> is strong, relaying history and life lessons through storytelling, poetry and song. Imigani, indirimbo, amazina and ivyivugo are literary genres in Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Basketball and track and field are noted sports. Martial arts are popular, as well. There are five major judo clubs: Club Judo de l'Entente Sportive, in Downtown, and four others throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is a popular pastime throughout the country, as are <a href="/wiki/Mancala" title="Mancala">mancala</a> games. </p>
      <p>Most Christian holidays are celebrated, with Christmas being the largest.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Burundian Independence Day is celebrated annually on 1 July.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> In 2005, the Burundian government declared <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, an Islamic holiday, to be a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-Burundi_celebrates_Muslim_holiday_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burundi_celebrates_Muslim_holiday-143">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Burundi" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Burundi">Media of Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2018</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="group of children at school in white shirt and khaki shorts uniforms" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg/220px-Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg/330px-Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg/440px-Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carolus_Magnus_Schule-Burundi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Carolus Magnus School in Burundi. The school benefits from the campaign "Your Day for Africa" by Aktion Tagwerk.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Burundi" title="Education in Burundi">Education in Burundi</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2009, the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate in Burundi was estimated to be 67% (73% male and 61% female), with a literacy rate of 77% and 76%, respectively, for men and women between the ages of 15 to 24.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> By 2015, this had increased to 85.6% (88.2% male and 83.1% female).<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> Literacy among adult women has increased by 17% since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> Burundi's literacy rate is relatively low due to low school attendance and because literacy in Kirundi only provides access to materials printed in that language, though it is higher than many other African countries. Ten percent of Burundian boys are allowed a secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burundi has one public university, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Burundi" title="University of Burundi">University of Burundi</a>. There are museums in the cities, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi_Geological_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Burundi Geological Museum (page does not exist)">Burundi Geological Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bujumbura" title="Bujumbura">Bujumbura</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Burundi_National_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Burundi National Museum">Burundi National Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Burundi_Museum_of_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="Burundi Museum of Life">Burundi Museum of Life</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gitega" title="Gitega">Gitega</a>. </p>
      <p>There will be a new school opening in one of the poorest regions, Rusaga, funded by an English charity, the Burundi Education Foundation. The Burundi Education Foundation was hoping to open the school in the summer of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010 a new elementary school was opened in the small village of Rwoga that is funded by the pupils of Westwood High School, Quebec, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Burundi.svg/32px-Flag_of_Burundi.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="19" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Burundi.svg/48px-Flag_of_Burundi.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Burundi.svg/64px-Flag_of_Burundi.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Burundi" title="Portal:Burundi">Burundi portal</a></span></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burundi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>

         <li id="cite_note-central_cities-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-central_cities_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-central_cities_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">While Gitega has been established as the political capital, Bujumbura is still the seat of the government and economic capital.</span> </li>

                  <tbody>
